        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acsami.1c18755"><meta property="og:title" content="Ultrahigh Rate and Ultralong Life Span Sodium Storage of FePS3 Enabled by the Space Confinement Effect of Layered Expanded Graphite"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/asset/images/acsami.1c18755.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="Metal phosphorus trichalcogenides have been regarded as promising high-capacity anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) owing to their high reversible capacity. Nevertheless, their practical application is plagued by poor diffusion kinetics and dramatic volume fluctuations during the charge–discharge process, resulting in no satisfactory rate and life span so far. Herein, we propose a space-confinement strategy to remarkably promote the cycling stability and rate capacity by embedding FePS3 particles in the interlayer of expanded graphite (EG), which are derived from in situ transformation of graphite intercalation compounds. The layered EG not only greatly alleviates the volume fluctuations of FePS3 by the space confinement effect so as to maintain the stability of the electrode microstructure, but it also ensures rapid Na+ and electron transfer during cycling. When acting as an anode for SIBs, the hybrid electrode delivers a highly reversible capacity of 312.5 mAh g–1 at an ultrahigh rate of 50 A g–1 while retaining an ultralong life span of 1300 cycles with a retention of 82.4% at 10 A g–1. Moreover, the excellent performance of the assembled full battery indicates the practical application potential of FPS/EG."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/asset/images/acsami.1c18755.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/nwyw~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="90da88db08c3b325-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da88db08c3b325-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: '0fddc2c7-5037-45a0-bcbe-690c7dbfa6b1'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

        <script async="" type="text/javascript" src="https://www.googletagservices.com/tag/js/gpt.js" rel="preconnect" nonce="90da88db08c3b325-SJC"></script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da88db08c3b325-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'applied_materials_interfaces';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

<script nonce="90da88db08c3b325-SJC">
$(function() {
    var serialCode = "aamick";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Ultrahigh Rate and Ultralong Life Span Sodium Storage of FePS&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Enabled by the Space Confinement Effect of Layered Expanded Graphite", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c18755", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Ultrahigh Rate and Ultralong Life Span Sodium Storage of FePS&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Enabled by the Space Confinement Effect of Layered Expanded Graphite", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c18755", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Ultrahigh Rate and Ultralong Life Span Sodium Storage of FePS&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Enabled by the Space Confinement Effect of Layered Expanded Graphite", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c18755", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Ultrahigh Rate and Ultralong Life Span Sodium Storage of FePS&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Enabled by the Space Confinement Effect of Layered Expanded Graphite", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c18755", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Ultrahigh Rate and Ultralong Life Span Sodium Storage of FePS&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Enabled by the Space Confinement Effect of Layered Expanded Graphite", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c18755", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Ultrahigh Rate and Ultralong Life Span Sodium Storage of FePS&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Enabled by the Space Confinement Effect of Layered Expanded Graphite", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c18755", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Ultrahigh Rate and Ultralong Life Span Sodium Storage of FePS&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Enabled by the Space Confinement Effect of Layered Expanded Graphite", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c18755", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Ultrahigh Rate and Ultralong Life Span Sodium Storage of FePS&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Enabled by the Space Confinement Effect of Layered Expanded Graphite", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c18755", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Ultrahigh Rate and Ultralong Life Span Sodium Storage of FePS&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Enabled by the Space Confinement Effect of Layered Expanded Graphite", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c18755", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

Tang</a></span></div></div></div></span></li><li><span><span class="hlFld-ContribAuthor" tabindex="0" data-id="article_author_info" property="author">Cheng Chao Li</span><strong>*</strong><div data-id="article_author_search">Cheng Chao Li</a></span></div><div class="loa-info-orcid"><img height="20" width="27" class="article_rightPermissionsLink"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone4" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone4"><div class="articleRightsPermissionsLink"><a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D55254%26pageCount%3D9%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DSong%2BHuang%252C%2BMinghui%2BYe%252C%2BYufei%2BZhang%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D13%26issueNum%3D46%26contentID%3Dacsami.1c18755%26title%3DUltrahigh%2BRate%2Band%2BUltralong%2BLife%2BSpan%2BSodium%2BStorage%2Bof%2BFePS3%2BEnabled%2Bby%2Bthe%2BSpace%2BConfinement%2BEffect%2Bof%2BLayered%2BExpanded%2BGraphite%26numPages%3D9%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D55262%26publicationDate%3DNovember%2B2021" Empty dropzone --></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="_i1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/asset/images/medium/am1c18755_0009.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/asset/images/large/am1c18755_0009.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c18755&amp;id=_i1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">Metal phosphorus trichalcogenides have been regarded as promising high-capacity anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) owing to their high reversible capacity. Nevertheless, their practical application is plagued by poor diffusion kinetics and dramatic volume fluctuations during the charge–discharge process, resulting in no satisfactory rate and life span so far. Herein, we propose a space-confinement strategy to remarkably promote the cycling stability and rate capacity by embedding FePS<sub>3</sub> particles in the interlayer of expanded graphite (EG), which are derived from <i>in situ</i> transformation of graphite intercalation compounds. The layered EG not only greatly alleviates the volume fluctuations of FePS<sub>3</sub> by the space confinement effect so as to maintain the stability of the electrode microstructure, but it also ensures rapid Na<sup>+</sup> and electron transfer during cycling. When acting as an anode for SIBs, the hybrid electrode delivers a highly reversible capacity of 312.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at an ultrahigh rate of 50 A g<sup>–1</sup> while retaining an ultralong life span of 1300 cycles with a retention of 82.4% at 10 A g<sup>–1</sup>. Moreover, the excellent performance of the assembled full battery indicates the practical application potential of FPS/EG.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D55254%26pageCount%3D9%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DSong%2BHuang%252C%2BMinghui%2BYe%252C%2BYufei%2BZhang%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D13%26issueNum%3D46%26contentID%3Dacsami.1c18755%26title%3DUltrahigh%2BRate%2Band%2BUltralong%2BLife%2BSpan%2BSodium%2BStorage%2Bof%2BFePS3%2BEnabled%2Bby%2Bthe%2BSpace%2BConfinement%2BEffect%2Bof%2BLayered%2BExpanded%2BGraphite%26numPages%3D9%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D55262%26publicationDate%3DNovember%2B2021" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2021 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291442&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Anode materials" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Anode%20materials" class="article__tags__link">Anode materials</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291517&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Batteries" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Batteries" class="article__tags__link">Batteries</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291371&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrodes" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Electrodes" class="article__tags__link">Electrodes</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291688&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Layered materials" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Layered%20materials" class="article__tags__link">Layered materials</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292506&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Materials" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Materials" class="article__tags__link">Materials</a></li></ul></div></div></div></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--keywords hlFld-Abstract"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Keywords</h3><div class="article__tags__tooltip" tabindex="0"><div class="article__tags__icon" aria-describedby="tooltip-keywords"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are keywords</span></div><p class="article__tags__diff" id="tooltip-keywords" role="tooltip">
                        Article keywords are supplied by the authors and highlight key terms and topics
                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Feps3&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_FePS3">FePS<sub>3</sub></a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Expanded+Graphite&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_expanded%20graphite">expanded graphite</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=In+Situ+Conversion&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_in%20situ%20conversion"><i>in situ</i> conversion</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Sodium+Ion+Battery&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_sodium%20ion%20battery">sodium ion battery</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Ultrahigh+Rate&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_ultrahigh%20rate">ultrahigh rate</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody" style="width: 384px;"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">1.  Introduction</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">Lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) have gradually occupied the main battery market to replace lead-acid batteries due to their long life span, high output voltage, and so forth. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref1 ref2 ref3'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2 ref3" aria-label="reference 1 to 3">(1−3)</a> However, the uneven global distribution and scarcity of lithium resources have brought concerns in terms of the sustainable development of LIBs. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4 ref5'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref4 ref5" aria-label="reference 4 and 5">(4,5)</a> In this context, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have regained the focus of research by virtue of their ample resources and similar intercalation/de-intercalation mechanism comparable to LIBs. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref6" aria-label="reference 6">(6)</a> More importantly, the lower cost and higher security of SIBs as well as the stronger environmental adaptability than LIBs make them potential new generation energy storage devices, especially in large-scale storage systems. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref7" aria-label="reference 7">(7)</a> Unfortunately, the larger Na<sup>+</sup> diameter determines their slow kinetics, which causes SIBs of the same material to deliver a worse rate performance or lower capacity than LIBs. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8 ref9 ref10'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref8 ref9 ref10" aria-label="reference 8 to 10">(8−10)</a> Furthermore, fast charging capacity has gradually become a necessary performance in various handheld electronic devices and even electric vehicles, which requires a high-rate/capacity anode material for SIBs. Therefore, it is still an urgent and challenging task to seek anode materials with a high rate and a high Na<sup>+</sup> storage capacity for SIBs. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref11" aria-label="reference 11">(11)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">Among various anode materials for SIBs, conversion materials based on transform reactions have aroused much interest owing to their higher Na<sup>+</sup> storage capacity. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref12" aria-label="reference 12">(12)</a> For example, FePS<sub>3</sub>, a typical conversion material, has a high theoretical capacity of 1318 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> due to the existence of high-capacity <i>P</i>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13 ref14 ref15'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref13 ref14 ref15" aria-label="reference 13 to 15">(13−15)</a> Additionally, the finer conductivity (10<sup>–5</sup> S m<sup>–1</sup>) of FePS<sub>3</sub> than traditional conversion materials (sulfides, oxides, etc.) and a larger interlayer spacing (6.4 Å) than the Na<sup>+</sup> radius (0.98 Å) make it possible for FePS<sub>3</sub> to become a high-rate anode. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16 ref17'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref16 ref17" aria-label="reference 16 and 17">(16,17)</a> However, FePS<sub>3</sub> tends to form bulk particles along the c-axis due to its internal layered crystal structure, greatly hindering the internal transportation of Na<sup>+</sup>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18" aria-label="reference 18">(18)</a> Engineering nano-scale particles or nano-architectures (such as foamy, layered, and so forth) is considered a resultful method to generate rapid ion diffusion. FePS<sub>3</sub> nanosheets with a lateral size of about 200 nm and a thickness of 18 nm were designed by Yan’s team. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref19" aria-label="reference 19">(19)</a> Such nanosheets deliver the most excellent capacity of 383 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 5 A g<sup>–1</sup> for SIBs. However, the fragile nanoarchitectures will easily collapse due to repeated volume fluctuation during electrochemical conversion, resulting in poor stability. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref20" aria-label="reference 20">(20)</a> The electrodes composed of nano-scale materials possess a decreasing volumetric energy density led by the small packing density, and the nano-scale synthesis generally involves harsh conditions, is time-consuming, and has a high cost, restricting its practical industrial application. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21" aria-label="reference 21">(21)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">Another obstacle to achieving the long life span of FePS<sub>3</sub> is the severe volume fluctuation during electrode conversion, contributing to cracking and pulverization of FePS<sub>3</sub>. The conduction of electrons is thus interrupted and the ion transportation path is lengthened by pulverized particles. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref22" aria-label="reference 22">(22)</a> Considering these obstacles, strategies such as the exfoliated FePS<sub>3</sub> compositing with graphene <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23" aria-label="reference 23">(23)</a> or MXene <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref13" aria-label="reference 13">(13)</a> and coating carbon <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref24" aria-label="reference 24">(24)</a> have been adopted, but so far, there is no satisfactory long-cycle stability. To alleviate effectively the stress generated by FePS<sub>3</sub>, a composite matrix with a strong mechanical toughness is required. As a derivative of graphite, expanded graphite (EG) possesses a stronger mechanical toughness than graphene by virtue of its interlayer van der Waals force. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref25" aria-label="reference 25">(25)</a> The active materials are embedded more easily in EG than in graphite due to the larger interlayer spacing of EG. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26" aria-label="reference 26">(26)</a> Nevertheless, the synthetic strategies for embedding active materials in the interlayer of EG are still rare. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref27" aria-label="reference 27">(27)</a> Therefore, the design of an SIB anode simultaneously featuring a high rate along with a high Na<sup>+</sup> storage capacity and a satisfactory life span is still a great challenge to be solved. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28" aria-label="reference 28">(28)</a></div><div class="NLM_p last">In this work, the space confinement effect and <i>in situ</i> conversion reaction are employed to construct evenly distributed FePS<sub>3</sub> particles embedded in the EG interlayer (denoted as FPS/EG) using stage-1 FeCl<sub>3</sub>/EG as the precursor. The space confinement of EG not only enables FePS<sub>3</sub> particles to achieve a smaller lateral size, which ensures rapid transportation of Na<sup>+</sup> and electrons, but it also alleviates the volume fluctuations of FePS<sub>3</sub> during cycling. Meanwhile, the conductive channel of EG further accelerates the transportation of electrons and Na<sup>+</sup>, contributing to the preeminent rate and cycling performance. When employed as the anode of SIBs, FPS/EG delivered 312.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> even at 50 A g<sup>–1</sup>, corresponding to a short duration of 44 s per cycle. The unprecedented cycling stability of up to 1300 cycles with a retention of 82.4% is achieved at 10 A g<sup>–1</sup>. The ultrahigh rate and ultralong cycle performance were achieved for the first time in the previously reported related materials for SIBs. Also, <i>in situ</i> X-ray diffraction (XRD) was employed to reveal the electrochemical conversion mechanism of FPS/EG. In the assembled sodium-ion full battery (FPS/EG||NVPO@C), the excellent performance indicates the potential practical application prospects of FPS/EG.</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i3">2.  Results and Discussion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec2_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i4" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i4">2.1.  Synthesis and Characterization of the FPS/EG Composite</h3><div class="NLM_p">The synthesis process of FePS<sub>3</sub> embedded in EG via intercalation and <i>in situ</i> conversion reaction is shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>. Prior to this, EG is first expanded to be obtained from expandable graphite at a high temperature, where a microwave tube furnace was used for heating to achieve greater expansion. Then, ferric chloride diffuses into the EG layer at 400 °C to prepare stage-1 FeCl<sub>3</sub>/EG, which was certified by the XRD pattern (Figure S1, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/suppl_file/am1c18755_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>), corresponding to previous reports. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29 ref30'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref29 ref30" aria-label="reference 29 and 30">(29,30)</a> Finally, stage-1 FeCl<sub>3</sub>/EG was further converted into an FePS<sub>3</sub>/EG composite <i>in situ</i> by phosphorization and sulfidation reaction. FePS<sub>3</sub> is well confined in the EG interlayers during <i>in situ</i> conversion because FeCl<sub>3</sub>/EG has a stage-1 structure (i.e., one layer of FeCl<sub>3</sub> and one layer of EG are stacked on each other). The XRD pattern of the FPS/EG composite indicated that all diffraction peaks were in good agreement with FePS<sub>3</sub> with a monoclinic structure (space group: <i>C</i>2/<i>m</i>), except a peak located at 26.6° that belonged to the signal of EG (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>a). Scanning electron microscopy (SEM) images indicated that FePS<sub>3</sub> particles with smaller lateral sizes are embedded in the interlayer of EG (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>b,c). The space confinement of EG prevents the excessive growth and aggregate of FePS<sub>3</sub> particles to create a convenient Na<sup>+</sup> transportation channel. However, pure FPS generates bulk particles due to overgrowth and inability to disperse (Figure S2, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/suppl_file/am1c18755_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>). The corresponding elemental mapping images manifested the uniform distribution of C, Fe, S, and P elements within FPS/EG (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>g). Similarly, transportation electron microscopy (TEM) images of FPS/EG also showed that FePS<sub>3</sub> particles were confined in the interlayer of EG (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>d). The microstructure of FPS/EG was also revealed through high-resolution TEM. The evident lattice spacing of 2.92 nm can be found, corresponding to the (130) plane of FePS<sub>3</sub> (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures 2</a>e,f and S3, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/suppl_file/am1c18755_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>).</div><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/asset/images/medium/am1c18755_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/asset/images/large/am1c18755_0002.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. Synthetic diagram of the FPS/EG composite via intercalation and <i>in situ</i> conversion reaction.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/asset/images/large/am1c18755_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c18755&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><figure id="fig2" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/asset/images/medium/am1c18755_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/asset/images/large/am1c18755_0003.jpeg" id="gr2" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. Characterization and microstructure of FPS/EG. (a) XRD patterns of FPS/EG and pure FPS. (b,c) SEM images and (d–f) TEM images of FPS/EG. (g) SEM and corresponding EDS images of FPS/EG.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/asset/images/large/am1c18755_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c18755&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">A X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) spectrum revealed that the FPS/EG composite possessed four elements of Fe, P, S, and C (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>a). In a high-solution Fe 2p spectrum, four peaks located at 709.6/723.2 and 714.6/730.0 eV were assigned to Fe<sup>2+</sup> and Fe<sup>3+</sup>, respectively (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>b). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref31" aria-label="reference 31">(31)</a> Two obvious peaks of the P 2p spectrum at 131.1 and 132.1 eV were distinguished as a P–S bond, and another wide peak at 134.1 eV was assigned as a P–O bond, resulting from oxidized P species in the atmosphere (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>c). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32 ref33'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32 ref33" aria-label="reference 32 and 33">(32,33)</a> The S 2p spectrum could be fitted into two parts at 163.8 and 162.7 eV, corresponding to S 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and S 2p<sub>1/2</sub>, respectively (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>d). In the C 1s spectrum, three peaks at 284.8, 285.3, and 287.5 eV were distinguished as C–C/C═C, C–O, and C═O bonds, respectively, attributed to the oxygen-containing functional group on EG. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34 ref35'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref34 ref35" aria-label="reference 34 and 35">(34,35)</a> Raman spectroscopy was performed to further compare the properties of FPS/EG and pure FPS (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>f). The two peaks found at 222.6 and 277.2 cm<sup>–1</sup> in line with the E<sub>g</sub> mode represent the vibration of the inner plane in the P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>6</sub> units. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref36" aria-label="reference 36">(36)</a> Meanwhile, the other two distinct peaks located at 246.9 and 378 cm<sup>–1</sup> were related to A<sub>1g</sub> modes, representing the outer-plane vibration of the P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>6</sub> units. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref37" aria-label="reference 37">(37)</a> What is interesting is that an obvious contrast peak between FPS/EG and FPS is located at 156 cm<sup>–1</sup>, which belongs to the E<sub>u</sub> mode of the P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>6</sub> units and originates from the vibration of the outer plane between adjacent P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>6</sub> units. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38 ref39 ref40'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref38 ref39 ref40" aria-label="reference 38 to 40">(38−40)</a> The peak intensity of the very weak E<sub>u</sub> mode of FPS/EG indicates that it has a thinner FePS<sub>3</sub> layer than pure FPS. This result is consistent with the SEM morphology of FPS/EG observed above. In addition, two distinct peaks at 1336 and 1583 cm<sup>–1</sup> are related to D and G bands of graphite, respectively. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref40" aria-label="reference 40">(40)</a> The low-intensity ratio of the D band to the G band (0.2) indicates that there are less disorders and defects in EG. To confirm the carbon content in FPS/EG, thermogravimetric analysis (TGA) was conducted in an air atmosphere (Figure S4, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/suppl_file/am1c18755_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>). The weight loss below 200 °C is due to the evaporation of the surface water and the crystal water of FPS/EG. The obvious mass loss at 450 °C is attributed to the loss of SO<sub>2</sub> after FePS<sub>3</sub> starts to be oxidized. EG starts to be oxidized at approximately 700 °C, leading to accelerated mass loss at this time. After calculations, the contents of FePS<sub>3</sub> and EG are 65.4 and 34.6%, respectively.</div><figure id="fig3" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/asset/images/medium/am1c18755_0004.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/asset/images/large/am1c18755_0004.jpeg" id="gr3" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. Electron state and bonding configuration of FPS/EG. (a) XPS spectra of the survey for the FPS/EG composite. (b) High-resolution Fe 2p (b), P 2p (c), S 2p (d), and C 1s (e) spectra of the FPS/EG composite. (f) Raman spectra of FPS/EG and pure FPS.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/asset/images/large/am1c18755_0004.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c18755&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div><div id="sec2_2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i5" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i5">2.2.  Electrochemical Performance of the FPS/EG Electrode in Half-Cells</h3><div class="NLM_p">The electrochemical performances of the FPS/EG composite and pure FPS are evaluated when they function as the anode of SIBs (Na sheets as the counter electrode and the reference electrode) via various electrochemical tests (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>). The CV curves of FPS/EG with different cycles were obtained and were between 0.01 and 2.8 V at a sweep speed of 0.2 mV s<sup>–1</sup>, as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>a. For the initial cathodic scan, an obvious peak at 1.43 V could be due to the insertion of Na<sup>+</sup> to form Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>FePS<sub>3</sub>. The peak of 1.1 V originates from the irreversible fracture of the P–S bond to form P and Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>FeS<sub>3</sub>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23" aria-label="reference 23">(23)</a> Two peaks of 0.75 and 0.26 V indicate a multi-step sodiation of P and Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>FeS<sub>3</sub> to generate Na<sub>3</sub>P, Fe, and Na<sub>2</sub>S. The small peak is located at 0.16 V and could result from the generation of an irreversible solid electrolyte interface (SEI) film. In the charging process, three oxidation peaks of 0.78, 1.53, and 2.07 V indicate a multistep desodiation to form Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>FeS<sub>3</sub> and P. Particularly worth mentioning is that FePS<sub>3</sub> cannot be reformed due to the irreversible fracture of the P–S bond. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref24" aria-label="reference 24">(24)</a> In subsequent cycles, the reversible conversion of Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>FeS<sub>3</sub> and P provides capacity. Moreover, <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>b shows the galvanostatic charge–discharge (GCD) profiles of the FPS/EG composite. The initial discharge capacity of 787.9 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> is obtained at 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup> with a Coulombic efficiency of 79.7%. The capacity loss of the initial cycle is principally due to the irreversible electrochemical conversion and the generation of an irreversible SEI film. Furthermore, the platform of the charge–discharge profiles and the peak position of the CV curve have a good consistency. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>c shows the long-cycle performance of FPS/EG. After 500 cycles, FPS/EG still has a reversible capacity of 456.9 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup> with a retention of 77.1%. However, an evident capacity decay began to appear after 180 cycles of the pure FPS sample, resulting from the drastic volume expansion of the electrode to generate a structural collapse. With the continuous fragmentation of the pure FPS particles, more active sites are exposed and the so-called “activation process” occurs, leading to an increase in the capacity, but it soon began to decay. The FePS<sub>3</sub> particles in the FPS/EG electrode maintain a relatively stable capacity under the protection of EG. Moreover, after 100 cycles, FPS/EG obtained 627.6 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> without a decline at 0.2 A g<sup>–1</sup> (Figure S5, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/suppl_file/am1c18755_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>). The rate performances of FPS/EG and pure FPS are shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>d,e. The FPS/EG electrode delivered high capacities of 649.3, 536.5, 503.7, 476.5, 442.8, 411.4, 377.8, and 351.0 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at the rates of 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, 5, 10, 20, and 30 A g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively. What is impressive is that FPS/EG still delivers a capacity of 312.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> even at an ultrahigh rate of 50 A g<sup>–1</sup>, corresponding to 44 s per cycle. Such a high rate in FPS/EG derived from confined FePS<sub>3</sub> particles in the EG interlayer contributes to a shortening in the transport pathways of Na<sup>+</sup> and the electrons. On the contrary, pure FPS delivers a significantly lower capacity owing to the aggregation and bulk particles, especially at high rates, compared with FPS/EG. Also, even at a high rate of 10 A g<sup>–1</sup>, FPS/EG still achieved a capacity of 322.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> with a retention of 82.4% after 1300 cycles (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>g), exhibiting excellent long-cycle stability. The space confinement of EG maintains the stable structure of FePS<sub>3</sub> during the electrochemical conversion process to contribute to an ultralong lifespan. However, the lower capacity of pure FPS is delivered and results in a capacity fluctuation at the end, which could be considered as a structural collapse. It is worth mentioning that ultrahigh rate and ultralong cycling performances of FPS/EG are achieved for the first time in similar materials previously reported. Besides, the electrochemical performance of EG is displayed in Figure S6, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/suppl_file/am1c18755_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information.</a> The capacity contribution of EG is negligible due to the low content. Finally, compared with the same type of material for SIBs, this work is in an advantageous position in terms of the capacity and the rate, demonstrating the outstanding performance of FPS/EG (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>f). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23 ref24 ref32 ref33 ref41 ref42 ref43'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23 ref24 ref32 ref33 ref41 ref42 ref43" aria-label="reference 23, 24, 32, 33 and 41 to 43">(23,24,32,33,41−43)</a></div><figure id="fig4" data-index="4" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 4</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/asset/images/medium/am1c18755_0005.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/asset/images/large/am1c18755_0005.jpeg" id="gr4" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 4. Electrochemical tests of the FPS/EG electrode for SIBs. (a) CV curves of different cycles at 0.2 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. (b) GCD curves of the FPS/EG electrode at 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup>. (c) Long-cycle performances of the FPS/EG and pure FPS electrodes at 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup>. (d) Rate performances of the FPS/EG and pure FPS electrodes. (e) GCD curves of the FPS/EG electrode at different rates. (f) Rate-capability comparisons between the FPS/EG electrodes and other similar materials previously reported. (g) Long-cycle performances of the FPS/EG and pure FPS electrodes at 10 A g<sup>–1</sup>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/asset/images/large/am1c18755_0005.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c18755&amp;id=fig4"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">The Na<sup>+</sup> storage behavior in the FPS/EG anode was further investigated to understand its internal kinetics as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>. The CV curves of FPS/EG at different sweep speeds between 0.01 and 2.8 V are shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>a. Four peaks can be found, in which every peak exhibits similar shapes with the augmenting of the sweep rate. It is well known that the peak current (<i>i</i>) and scan speed (<i>v</i>) of the CV at different scan speeds possess the following relationship: <i>i</i> = <i>av</i><sup><i>b</i></sup>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44 ref45'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref44 ref45" aria-label="reference 44 and 45">(44,45)</a> Based on this, a straight line with a slope of the <i>b</i> value can be obtained, which is used to characterize the kinetic type of Na<sup>+</sup> in FPS/EG. When the <i>b</i> value is closer to 0.5, it means that the transportation of Na<sup>+</sup> belongs to diffusion control, whereas a <i>b</i> value closer to 1 indicates that it is a process that is capacitance-dominated. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>b reveals the relationship between the peak current and the sweep rate. The <i>b</i> values of peak 1 to peak 4 are 0.86, 0.99, 0.74, and 0.94, respectively, meaning that the transportation of Na<sup>+</sup> is a capacitance-dominated process. Furthermore, the proportion of capacitance and the diffusion process are calculated via the following relationship: <i>i</i> = <i>k</i><sub>1</sub><i>v</i> + <i>k</i><sub>2</sub><i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45 ref46'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref45 ref46" aria-label="reference 45 and 46">(45,46)</a> The capacitance contribution of 84.2% of the FPS/EG electrode can be obtained at 0.5 mV s<sup>–1</sup> (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>c). The capacitance contributions from 51.1 to 84.2% are achieved at scanning speeds of 0.2–5 mV s<sup>–1</sup>, respectively (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>d). The high capacitance contributions at different scanning speeds are conducive to the excellent rate performance of FPS/EG. To further understand the reasons for the difference in performances between FPS/EG and pure FPS, their electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) was tested (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>e). The concave semicircle of the EIS curve in the high-frequency region represents the charge-transfer resistance (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>). Compared with pure FPS, an evident smaller <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> is found in the FPS/EG electrode, which is also the reason for its better rate performance. Moreover, according to the formula <i>Z</i>′ = <i>R</i> + σω<sup>–1/2</sup>, where <i>Z</i>′, <i>R</i>, σ, and ω represent the real part of impedance, total resistance, Warburg coefficient, and angular velocity, respectively, the Warburg coefficients (σ) can be obtained. The Warburg coefficients (σ) of FPS/EG and pure FPS were calculated and were 33.4 and 147.1, respectively. The smaller Warburg coefficient of FPS/EG indicates its faster diffusion of Na<sup>+</sup> (Figure S7, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/suppl_file/am1c18755_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>). These results once again confirm that FePS<sub>3</sub> confined in EG possesses faster Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics, contributing to the ultrahigh rate capacity. The EIS plots of different cycles are tested to further understand the excellent performance of FPS/EG shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>f. The smaller <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> after the 30th cycle compared to that of the 10th cycle may be because the process of sodiation/desodiation reduces the resistance of charge transportation. As the number of cycles increased to 100 cycles, the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> gradually increased slightly and remained stable from 100 cycles to 150 cycles, which may be related to the formation of the SEI film and the gradual stabilization.</div><figure id="fig5" data-index="5" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 5</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/asset/images/medium/am1c18755_0006.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/asset/images/large/am1c18755_0006.jpeg" id="gr5" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 5. Kinetic analysis of FPS/EG. (a) CV curves at different scan rates. (b) Calculation of the <i>b</i>-value employing the relation between the peak current and the scan rate. (c) Separation of the capacitive (dotted area) and diffusion currents at 5 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. (d) Capacitive contribution rates at different scan rates. (e) EIS plots of FPS/EG and pure FPS. (f) EIS plots of different cycles of FPS/EG.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/asset/images/large/am1c18755_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c18755&amp;id=fig5"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div><div id="sec2_3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i6" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i6">2.3.  Investigation of the Conversion Mechanism for FPS/EG during Cycling</h3><div class="NLM_p">The mechanism of electrochemical conversion was researched via <i>in situ</i> XRD (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>). At the beginning of the discharge, the obvious diffraction peaks are located at approximately 28.0 and 57.5°, corresponding to the characteristic peak of FePS<sub>3</sub>. After that, these two diffraction peaks gradually weaken, which could be derived from the intercalation of Na<sup>+</sup> to the FePS<sub>3</sub> crystal structure. When charging to 1.1 V, the two distinct peaks simultaneously appearing at about 24.0 and 22.6° are related to the characteristic peaks of P and Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>FeS<sub>3</sub>, respectively, which are generated from the break of the P–S bond in Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>FePS<sub>3</sub>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23 ref24'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23 ref24" aria-label="reference 23 and 24">(23,24)</a> The subsequent attenuated phosphorus peak is due to further sodiation to form Na<sub>3</sub>P. At 0.75 V of discharging, a small peak began to appear at about 21.0°, corresponding to Na<sub>2</sub>S, which is derived from the further conversion of Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>FeS<sub>3</sub> to Fe and Na<sub>2</sub>S. The peak of Na<sub>2</sub>S gradually disappeared and the peak of Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>FeS<sub>3</sub> strengthened during charging, indicating the re-formation of Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>FeS<sub>3</sub>. What needs to be mentioned is that FePS<sub>3</sub> did not reappear at the end of charging, which results from the irreversible fracture of the P–S bond. It is inferred that unstable P–S bonds in FePS<sub>3</sub> are destroyed due to the insertion of Na<sup>+</sup> and cannot be reversibly restored in the electrolyte environment. In consequence, Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>FeS<sub>3</sub> and P are used as the active material for reversible conversion to provide capacity in the subsequent cycles. It should be noted that the absence of the P peak during charging and the Fe peak in the whole process could be due to the formation of amorphous or ultra-small-sized products. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41 ref47 ref48'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref41 ref47 ref48" aria-label="reference 41, 47 and 48">(41,47,48)</a> The entire reaction process equation of FePS<sub>3</sub> is described in the <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/suppl_file/am1c18755_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>. Interestingly, the characteristic peak of EG at approximately 26.6° gradually disappearing during discharging is attributed to the Na<sup>+</sup>–electrolyte co-intercalation phenomenon in the ether electrolyte. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref49'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref49" aria-label="reference 49">(49)</a> In the subsequent charging process, EG returned to the original state and the peak reappeared, which proved the good reversibility.</div><figure id="fig6" data-index="6" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 6</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/asset/images/medium/am1c18755_0007.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/asset/images/large/am1c18755_0007.jpeg" id="gr6" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 6. <i>In situ</i> XRD patterns for the initial cycle of the FPS/EG electrode.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/asset/images/large/am1c18755_0007.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c18755&amp;id=fig6"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div><div id="sec2_4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i7" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i7">2.4.  Electrochemical Characterization and Performance of the FPS/EG||NVPO@C Full Cells</h3><div class="NLM_p">Taking into account that the FPS/EG anode has an excellent Na<sup>+</sup> storage capacity in the half-cell along with a remarkable rate capacity (up to 50 A g<sup>–1</sup>) and long-cycle stability, we can foresee that it has great potential in SIBs. To confirm the possibility of its practical application, here, we match Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>@C (NVPO@C) as the cathode to assemble a full sodium ion battery (FPS/EG||NVPO@C) (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 7</a>a). NVPO@C was synthesized based on previous reports, and the related characterizations are exhibited in Figure S8, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/suppl_file/am1c18755_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50 ref51 ref52 ref53'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref50 ref51 ref52 ref53" aria-label="reference 50 to 53">(50−53)</a> The FPS/EG||NVPO@C full battery can have an output voltage of 2.3 V under the limitation of the cathode capacity with a voltage window of 1.1–3.5 V (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 7</a>b). Two such batteries in series can power the LED light. The excellent rate performance of the FPS/EG||NVPO@C full battery is shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 7</a>c,d. The capacities of 439.2, 415.1, 385.0, and 331.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> (based on the active mass of the anode) were delivered at the rates of 0.5, 1, 2, and 5 A g<sup>–1</sup>. Even at a high rate of 10 A g<sup>–1</sup>, it still has a specific capacity of 276.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>. When returning to 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup>, it still has a capacity of 407.7 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>, indicating good reversibility. Furthermore, there is almost no capacity decline after 100 cycles at 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup> (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 7</a>e). The energy density of the as-prepared FPS/EG||NVPO@C full battery is estimated to be 113.8 Wh kg<sup>–1</sup> at 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup> based on the total mass of active materials in both the anode and the cathode. The most important thing is that it still has a capacity of 281.7 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 400 cycles under 2 A g<sup>–1</sup> with a retention of 81.2%. These excellent performances show that FPS/EG||NVPO@C full battery has practical application possibilities.</div><figure id="fig7" data-index="7" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 7</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/asset/images/medium/am1c18755_0008.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/asset/images/large/am1c18755_0008.jpeg" id="gr7" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 7. Electrochemical performance of an FPS/EG||NVPO/C full cell. (a) Schematic diagram of a full battery. (b) GCD curves of the FPS/EG anode and the NVPO/C cathode at 0.2 A g<sup>–1</sup> (inset: photograph of the LED viewing screen powered by a two-series-connected FPS/EG||NVPO/C full cell). (c) GCD curves at different rates. (d) Rate performance. (e,f) Long cycling performance at 0.2 and 2 A g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/asset/images/large/am1c18755_0008.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c18755&amp;id=fig7"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div></div><div id="sec3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i8">3.  Conclusions</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p last">In summary, we successfully constructed FePS<sub>3</sub> particles embedded in the EG interlayer by combining the space confinement and <i>in situ</i> conversion reaction. The space confinement of EG enables FePS<sub>3</sub> particles to achieve a smaller lateral size. The small lateral distance and evenly dispersed particles in the EG interlayer ensure rapid transportation of Na<sup>+</sup> and the electrons. EG provides mechanical support for FePS<sub>3</sub> to alleviate the volume stress during cycling. Therefore, FPS/EG delivers a high capacity of 312.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> even at 50 A g<sup>–1</sup>. Furthermore, it still has a capacity of 322.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 1300 cycles at 10 A g<sup>–1</sup> with a retention of 82.4%. The ultrahigh rate and ultralong cycle performance have been achieved for the first time in similar materials for SIBs. Most importantly, the assembled FPS/EG||NVPO@C full battery achieved an excellent performance, indicating the potential practical applications of FPS/EG. Although this work has significantly improved performance, it can still further increase the proportion of FePS<sub>3</sub> and design smaller particles to maximize its capacity in FPS/EG.</div></div><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i9">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge at <a href="/doi/10.1021/acsami.1c18755?goto=supporting-info" class="ext-link">https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acsami.1c18755</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">XRD pattern and SEM images of pure FPS; calculation of d-spacing for FPS/EG; TGA curve for FPS/EG; long-cycling performance of FPS/EG at 0.2 A g<sup>–1</sup>; electrochemical performance of EG; relationship of the real part versus low frequencies of FPS/EG and pure FPS; and corresponding characterization of the NVPO@C cathode (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/suppl_file/am1c18755_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c18755/suppl_file/am1c18755_si_001.pdf">am1c18755_si_001.pdf (723.66 kb)</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="testing" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.1c18755" data-url="https://widgets.figshare.com/static/figshare.js" id="figshare-widget" style="display: block;"></div><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="85b54935-30e9-4058-a6d2-0b40fb754a85" class="mb-4">

                        cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sustainable Recycling Technology for Li-Ion Batteries and Beyond: Challenges and Future Prospects</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fan, Ersha; Li, Li; Wang, Zhenpo; Lin, Jiao; Huang, Yongxin; Yao, Ying; Chen, Renjie; Wu, Feng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Reviews (Washington, DC, United States)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">120</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">14</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7020-7063</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Tremendous efforts are being made to develop electrode materials, electrolytes, and separators for energy storage devices to meet the needs of emerging technologies such as elec. vehicles, decarbonized electricity, and electrochem. energy storage.  However, the sustainability concerns of lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and next-generation rechargeable batteries have received little attention.  Recycling plays an important role in the overall sustainability of future batteries and is affected by battery attributes including environmental hazards and the value of their constituent resources.  Therefore, recycling should be considered when developing battery systems.  Herein, a systematic overview is provided of rechargeable battery sustainability.  With a particular focus on elec. vehicles, the market competitiveness is analyzed of batteries in terms of economy, environment, and policy.  Considering the large vols. of batteries soon to be retired, the battery utilization and recycling are comprehensively evaluated from the perspectives of economic feasibility, environmental impact, technol., and safety.  Battery sustainability is discussed with respect to life-cycle assessment and analyzed from the perspectives of strategic resources and economic demand.  Finally, a 4H strategy is proposed for battery recycling with the aims of high efficiency, high economic return, high environmental benefit, and high safety.  New challenges and future prospects for battery sustainability are also highlighted.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoimlaAYAtENLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgQbUuzGUFQPQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhs1OmtLw%253D&amp;md5=e9d04bf0883e3a3e0931cba4328e492b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref2'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit2" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201703772"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nayak, P.
